### User Story — STORY-5.3: Edit own comment
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-5 → <EPIC-5-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-5; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As the author of a comment, I want to edit the body of my comment, so that I can correct mistakes or add information after posting.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Security / authz (layered): two checks enforced server-side in order — (1) caller is a board member with role Owner or Editor; (2) caller is the comment's author. Failure at (1): 403 (Viewer) or 404 (non-member) or 401. Failure at (2): 403. The board Owner does <b>not</b> have permission to edit another user's comment (edit = author-only; delete = author or board Owner).</li><li>Request body contract: the PUT endpoint accepts { body } ONLY (1–5000 characters). Fields such as authorId, createdAt, updatedAt, isEdited, or any other comment property are immutable — they are silently ignored even if present in the request body.</li><li>Validation: body 1–5000 characters, same constraint as STORY-5.1.</li><li>cardId scope: a cardId that does not belong to boardId returns 404 (existence not disclosed — consistent with STORY-5.1's cross-board guard).</li><li>Idempotency: re-submitting the same body is allowed and returns 200 (no 'nothing changed' error); isEdited is set to true and updatedAt updated on every successful edit.</li><li>API contract: PUT /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId}. Returns 200 with updated DTO. RFC 7807 on all error paths.</li><li>DTOs only at the boundary.</li><li>Clean Architecture: use-case in Application (receives callerId, performs authz); EF Core update in Infrastructure; thin controller in Api.</li><li>Optimistic locking: not required in v1 (last-write-wins acceptable for comments).</li><li>Accessibility: WCAG 2.2 AA — inline edit form has visible label, character counter, error via aria-describedby; cancel action keyboard-accessible (Esc cancels).</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Editing another user's comment (that is a 403, not a feature).</li><li>Edit history / revision log (deferred to future).</li><li>Markdown/rich-text editing.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.5, §1.4, §1.6, §2.2</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>author</b> of a comment and an active board member (Owner or Editor) <b>When</b> I PUT { body } (1–5000 characters) to /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId} <b>Then</b> the comment body is updated, updatedAt is refreshed, and I receive 200 OK with the updated comment DTO (same shape as STORY-5.1, isEdited: true).</p><p><b>Given</b> the comment is successfully edited <b>When</b> other members are connected <b>Then</b> they observe the updated body and 'Edited' indicator in real-time (propagation &lt;1 s via EPIC-6).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated but I am <b>not the author</b> of the comment <b>and</b> I am <b>not the board Owner</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to edit the comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 and the comment is not modified (ownership rule: only the author may edit their own comment; board Owner cannot edit another's comment, only delete it per STORY-5.4).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as a <b>Viewer</b> of the board (even if I were somehow the original author via a role change) <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 — Viewer role forbids all mutations.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am <b>not a member</b> of the board <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed).</p><p><b>Given</b> I present <b>no or invalid JWT</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 401 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> I submit an <b>empty body or one exceeding 5000 characters</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to edit <b>Then</b> I receive 400 RFC 7807 with a validation problem detail; the comment is not modified.</p><p><b>Given</b> the commentId does not exist or does not belong to cardId/boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to edit <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> the cardId does not belong to boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed — matching STORY-5.1's explicit cross-board guard).</p><p><b>Given</b> I send a PUT request body that includes fields other than body (e.g. authorId, createdAt) <b>When</b> the server processes the request <b>Then</b> those extra fields are silently ignored; only body (1–5000 characters) is accepted and updated; all other comment fields remain immutable.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am viewing a comment I authored <b>When</b> the card detail is rendered <b>Then</b> an <b>Edit</b> button/icon is visible on my comment (hidden from non-authors and Viewers); clicking it opens an inline edit form pre-populated with the current body; submitting saves and shows the updated text plus an 'Edited' badge; cancelling restores the original text without a network call; form meets <b>WCAG 2.2 AA</b>.</p>
```

**Create**
```

board Owner cannot edit another's comment, only delete it per STORY-5.4).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as a <b>Viewer</b> of the board (even if I were somehow the original author via a role change) <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 — Viewer role forbids all mutations.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am <b>not a member</b> of the board <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed).</p><p><b>Given</b> I present <b>no or invalid JWT</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 401 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> I submit an <b>empty body or one exceeding 5000 characters</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to edit <b>Then</b> I receive 400 RFC 7807 with a validation problem detail; the comment is not modified.</p><p><b>Given</b> the commentId does not exist or does not belong to cardId/boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to edit <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> the cardId does not belong to boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to edit a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed — matching STORY-5.1's explicit cross-board guard).</p><p><b>Given</b> I send a PUT request body that includes fields other than body (e.g. authorId, createdAt) <b>When</b> the server processes the request <b>Then</b> those extra fields are silently ignored; only body (1–5000 characters) is accepted and updated; all other comment fields remain immutable.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am viewing a comment I authored <b>When</b> the card detail is rendered <b>Then</b> an <b>Edit</b> button/icon is visible on my comment (hidden from non-authors and Viewers); clicking it opens an inline edit form pre-populated with the current body; submitting saves and shows the updated text plus an 'Edited' badge; cancelling restores the original text without a network call; form meets <b>WCAG 2.2 AA</b>.</p>"

### User Story — STORY-5.4: Delete a comment
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-5 → <EPIC-5-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-5; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As the author of a comment or the board Owner, I want to delete a comment, so that inaccurate or inappropriate content can be removed from the discussion.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Security / authz (layered): two checks enforced server-side in order — (1) caller is a board member; (2) caller is either the comment's author OR a board Owner. Failure at (1): 404 (non-member) or 401. Failure at (2): 403. Board Owner may delete <b>any</b> comment; no other role may delete a comment they do not own.</li><li>Destructive action — confirmation required: the UI must show a confirmation dialog before sending the DELETE request. No 'undo'. This applies to both the author and the board Owner paths.</li><li>Idempotency: a second DELETE on an already-deleted comment returns 404 (not 204); comment IDs are not reused.</li><li>API contract: DELETE /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId}. Returns 204 No Content on success. RFC 7807 on all error paths.</li><li>Clean Architecture: use-case in Application (receives callerId, performs authz); EF Core hard-delete in Infrastructure; thin controller in Api (no soft-delete in v1 — out of scope).</li><li>Cascades: deleting a comment removes only that comment; card and board are unaffected.</li><li>Accessibility: WCAG 2.2 AA — confirmation dialog has role='alertdialog', aria-labelledby, aria-describedby; focus moves into dialog on open; Esc cancels; focus returns to trigger element on close.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Soft-delete / restore / trash functionality (hard-delete only in v1).</li><li>Bulk delete of multiple comments.</li><li>Deleting all comments on a card in one action.</li><li>Audit trail of deleted comments (EPIC-7 activity feed tracks the deletion event, not this story).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.5, §1.4, §1.6, §2.2</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>author</b> of a comment (with role Owner or Editor) <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE to /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId} <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>board Owner</b> (but <b>not</b> the comment's author) <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content (board Owner may delete any comment on any card in that board).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>board Owner AND the comment's author</b> <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content (the author+Owner combination satisfies both the authorship path and the board Owner path; either alone is sufficient).</p><p><b>Given</b> the comment is successfully deleted <b>When</b> other members are connected <b>Then</b> the comment disappears in real-time (propagation &lt;1 s via EPIC-6) without a manual refresh.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as an <b>Editor who is not the comment's author</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to delete the comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 and the comment is not deleted (non-author, non-Owner editors cannot delete another user's comment).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as a <b>Viewer</b> (regardless of authorship) <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 and the comment is not deleted.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am <b>not a member</b> of the board <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed).</p><p><b>Given</b> I present <b>no or invalid JWT</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 401 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> the commentId does not exist or does not belong to cardId/boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to delete <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am the author or the board Owner viewing a comment <b>When</b> the card detail is rendered <b>Then</b> a <b>Delete</b> button/icon is visible on eligible comments (hidden from non-authors/non-Owners and Viewers); clicking it opens a <b>confirmation dialog</b> ('Delete this comment? This cannot be undone.') with Confirm and Cancel; confirming sends the DELETE request; cancelling closes the dialog without any network call; the UI meets <b>WCAG 2.2 AA</b> (modal focus trap, role='alertdialog', keyboard-dismissible).</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-5.4: Delete a comment" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-5; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As the author of a comment or the board Owner, I want to delete a comment, so that inaccurate or inappropriate content can be removed from the discussion.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Security / authz (layered): two checks enforced server-side in order — (1) caller is a board member; (2) caller is either the comment's author OR a board Owner. Failure at (1): 404 (non-member) or 401. Failure at (2): 403. Board Owner may delete any comment; no other role may delete a comment they do not own.</li><li>Destructive action — confirmation required: the UI must show a confirmation dialog before sending the DELETE request. No 'undo'. This applies to both the author and the board Owner paths.</li><li>Idempotency: a second DELETE on an already-deleted comment returns 404 (not 204); comment IDs are not reused.</li><li>API contract: DELETE /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId}. Returns 204 No Content on success. RFC 7807 on all error paths.</li><li>Clean Architecture: use-case in Application (receives callerId, performs authz); EF Core hard-delete in Infrastructure; thin controller in Api (no soft-delete in v1 — out of scope).</li><li>Cascades: deleting a comment removes only that comment; card and board are unaffected.</li><li>Accessibility: WCAG 2.2 AA — confirmation dialog has role='alertdialog', aria-labelledby, aria-describedby; focus moves into dialog on open; Esc cancels; focus returns to trigger element on close.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Soft-delete / restore / trash functionality (hard-delete only in v1).</li><li>Bulk delete of multiple comments.</li><li>Deleting all comments on a card in one action.</li><li>Audit trail of deleted comments (EPIC-7 activity feed tracks the deletion event, not this story).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.5, §1.4, §1.6, §2.2</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>author</b> of a comment (with role Owner or Editor) <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE to /api/boards/{boardId}/cards/{cardId}/comments/{commentId} <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>board Owner</b> (but <b>not</b> the comment's author) <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content (board Owner may delete any comment on any card in that board).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as the <b>board Owner AND the comment's author</b> <b>When</b> I confirm and send DELETE <b>Then</b> the comment is permanently deleted and I receive 204 No Content (the author+Owner combination satisfies both the authorship path and the board Owner path; either alone is sufficient).</p><p><b>Given</b> the comment is successfully deleted <b>When</b> other members are connected <b>Then</b> the comment disappears in real-time (propagation &lt;1 s via EPIC-6) without a manual refresh.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as an <b>Editor who is not the comment's author</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to delete the comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 and the comment is not deleted (non-author, non-Owner editors cannot delete another user's comment).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated as a <b>Viewer</b> (regardless of authorship) <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 403 RFC 7807 and the comment is not deleted.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am <b>not a member</b> of the board <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807 (existence not disclosed).</p><p><b>Given</b> I present <b>no or invalid JWT</b> <b>When</b> I attempt to delete a comment <b>Then</b> I receive 401 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> the commentId does not exist or does not belong to cardId/boardId <b>When</b> I attempt to delete <b>Then</b> I receive 404 RFC 7807.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am the author or the board Owner viewing a comment <b>When</b> the card detail is rendered <b>Then</b> a <b>Delete</b> button/icon is visible on eligible comments (hidden from non-authors/non-Owners and Viewers); clicking it opens a <b>confirmation dialog</b> ('Delete this comment? This cannot be undone.') with Confirm and Cancel; confirming sends the DELETE request; cancelling closes the dialog without any network call; the UI meets <b>WCAG 2.2 AA</b> (modal focus trap, role='alertdialog', keyboard-dismissible).</p>"
```

**Link to parent**
```
az boards work-item relation add --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --id <this-story-id> --relation-type parent --target-id <EPIC-5-id>
```
### User Story — STORY-6.1: Establish an authenticated real-time connection
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-6 → <EPIC-6-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-6; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As a board member, I want my browser to silently establish a real-time connection when I open a board and join that board's live-update group, so that I receive changes from other members instantly without refreshing.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Azure SignalR Default mode (§2.4, §2.9): negotiate endpoint routes through the API; the client then connects directly to the service. The API holds no client sockets; all API instances are equivalent (scale-out-safe; no sticky sessions required).</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): OnConnectedAsync validates the JWT via the standard ASP.NET Core [Authorize] attribute; JoinBoardAsync performs a server-side membership check (calls IBoardMembershipRepository or equivalent) before adding the caller to board-{boardId}. These checks are not bypassable client-side.</li><li>Clean Architecture: the hub lives in the Api layer and calls Application-layer services (no direct DB access in the hub; deps inward only).</li><li>Scale-out safety: no per-instance in-memory group state; Azure SignalR Service manages group membership — safe across multiple API instances.</li><li>SPA connection lifecycle: connect on board-view mount; reconnect with backoff; LeaveBoard + stop() on unmount. Managed in a composable (e.g. useBoardHub), not scattered across components.</li><li>Security: JWT forwarded as a query-string token on the WebSocket handshake (standard SignalR pattern); connection info from negotiate must not be cached client-side beyond the session.</li><li>Performance: negotiate round-trip must not add perceptible latency to the board-load critical path; connection is initiated in parallel with the initial board data fetch.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: the 'Reconnecting...' banner uses role='status' or aria-live='polite'; the 'Connecting...' badge is accessible; no color-only status signaling.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Broadcasting mutations (STORY-6.2–6.4).</li><li>Presence (which members are viewing — STORY-6.5).</li><li>Hub-to-client messages about board events (this story wires the connection only).</li><li>Push notifications when not viewing the board.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.4, §2.9</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> I am an authenticated board member <b>When</b> the board view mounts <b>Then</b> the SPA calls POST /hubs/board/negotiate (with my JWT), receives Azure SignalR connection info, and the @microsoft/signalr client connects directly to the Azure SignalR Service — the API holds no WebSocket socket.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SignalR connection is established <b>When</b> the SPA sends JoinBoard(boardId) via the hub <b>Then</b> the hub verifies server-side that the caller is a MEMBER of boardId; if valid the caller is added to group board-{boardId}; if not a member the hub returns an error and the client is not added to the group.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am unauthenticated (no token or expired token) <b>When</b> a connection is attempted <b>Then</b> the hub's OnConnectedAsync rejects the connection with 401; no group is joined.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated and in the board group <b>When</b> the SPA loses connectivity (network drop, container restart) <b>Then</b> the @microsoft/signalr client reconnects with exponential backoff (using .withAutomaticReconnect()); upon reconnect it re-sends JoinBoard(boardId) to re-join the group; the board view displays a transient 'Reconnecting...' banner during the outage.</p><p><b>Given</b> the reconnect banner is visible <b>When</b> the connection is restored <b>Then</b> the banner disappears and the board refreshes its data (one GET /boards/{id} full reload) to reconcile any changes missed during the outage.</p><p><b>Given</b> I navigate away from the board <b>When</b> the board view unmounts <b>Then</b> the SPA sends LeaveBoard(boardId), calls connection.stop(), and no further messages are received for that board.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA is loading the board and establishing the connection <b>When</b> the connection is not yet Connected <b>Then</b> a non-blocking loading indicator is shown in the board header (e.g. a small spinner or 'Connecting...' badge); the board's cached REST data renders immediately if available.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-6.1: Establish an authenticated real-time connection" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-6; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As a board member, I want my browser to silently establish a real-time connection when I open a board and join that board's live-update group, so that I receive changes from other members instantly without refreshing.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Azure SignalR Default mode (§2.4, §2.9): negotiate endpoint routes through the API; the client then connects directly to the service. The API holds no client sockets; all API instances are equivalent (scale-out-safe; no sticky sessions required).</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): OnConnectedAsync validates the JWT via the standard ASP.NET Core [Authorize] attribute; JoinBoardAsync performs a server-side membership check (calls IBoardMembershipRepository or equivalent) before adding the caller to board-{boardId}. These checks are not bypassable client-side.</li><li>Clean Architecture: the hub lives in the Api layer and calls Application-layer services (no direct DB access in the hub; deps inward only).</li><li>Scale-out safety: no per-instance in-memory group state; Azure SignalR Service manages group membership — safe across multiple API instances.</li><li>SPA connection lifecycle: connect on board-view mount; reconnect with backoff; LeaveBoard + stop() on unmount. connection is initiated in parallel with the initial board data fetch.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: the 'Reconnecting...' banner uses role='status' or aria-live='polite'; the 'Connecting...' badge is accessible; no color-only status signaling.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Broadcasting mutations (STORY-6.2–6.4).</li><li>Presence (which members are viewing — STORY-6.5).</li><li>Hub-to-client messages about board events (this story wires the connection only).</li><li>Push notifications when not viewing the board.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.4, §2.9</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> I am an authenticated board member <b>When</b> the board view mounts <b>Then</b> the SPA calls POST /hubs/board/negotiate (with my JWT), receives Azure SignalR connection info, and the @microsoft/signalr client connects directly to the Azure SignalR Service — the API holds no WebSocket socket.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SignalR connection is established <b>When</b> the SPA sends JoinBoard(boardId) via the hub <b>Then</b> the hub verifies server-side that the caller is a MEMBER of boardId; no group is joined.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am authenticated and in the board group <b>When</b> the SPA loses connectivity (network drop, container restart) <b>Then</b> the @microsoft/signalr client reconnects with exponential backoff (using .withAutomaticReconnect()); upon reconnect it re-sends JoinBoard(boardId) to re-join the group; the board view displays a transient 'Reconnecting...' banner during the outage.</p><p><b>Given</b> the reconnect banner is visible <b>When</b> the connection is restored <b>Then</b> the banner disappears and the board refreshes its data (one GET /boards/{id} full reload) to reconcile any changes missed during the outage.</p><p><b>Given</b> I navigate away from the board <b>When</b> the board view unmounts <b>Then</b> the SPA sends LeaveBoard(boardId), calls connection.stop(), and no further messages are received for that board.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA is loading the board and establishing the connection <b>When</b> the connection is not yet Connected <b>Then</b> a non-blocking loading indicator is shown in the board header (e.g. a small spinner or 'Connecting...' badge); the board's cached REST data renders immediately if available.</p>"

### User Story — STORY-6.2: Propagate card mutations to board group in real time
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-6 → <EPIC-6-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-6; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As a board member viewing a board, I want card changes made by other members (create, edit, move between lists, reorder, delete, and metadata updates) to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that I always see the current state of the board without manual intervention.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): from the moment the API persists the mutation to the moment the SignalR message is delivered to connected clients. The broadcast is issued by the Application layer (via IBoardEventPublisher) within the same request after the DB write commits; no async queue introduces extra latency.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): broadcast is addressed to group board-{boardId} via the Azure SignalR Service; any API instance can issue it; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): the IBoardEventPublisher interface lives in Application; its SignalR implementation lives in Infrastructure (IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;); command handlers call the publisher — no hub-to-handler dependency inversion.</li><li>Hub authorization (§EPIC-6 spine): only members of the board receive messages in board-{boardId}; server-side group membership (STORY-6.1) enforces this. No client-side filtering needed.</li><li>Message shape: each event carries a typed, versioned DTO (e.g. CardCreatedEvent, CardMovedEvent, CardDeletedEvent, CardMetadataUpdatedEvent). DTOs are defined in Application and serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency / last-write-wins: no OT or CRDT; the last persisted write wins. The SPA applies each incoming event to the Pinia store immutably (replace-in-place by id); stale events for deleted cards are silently dropped.</li><li>No self-echo: the broadcaster does not need to suppress delivery to the originating connection (Azure SignalR handles broadcasting to the group; if the originating client is in the group it will receive the event — the SPA store update must be idempotent to handle this).</li><li>Security / authorization: the publish call is inside the command handler, which already enforces role-based authorization (STORY-1.5); no additional auth on the publish path.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live card additions/removals/updates do not steal keyboard focus; an aria-live='polite' region announces significant changes (e.g. 'Card 'Deploy infra' moved to Done').</li><li>Card metadata fields propagated: label assignments, assignee, due date, priority (all EPIC-4 mutations). Each has its own event type to allow targeted store patching.</li><li>Events covered in this story: CardCreated, CardTitleUpdated, CardMoved, CardReordered, CardDeleted, CardLabelAssigned, CardLabelRemoved, CardAssigneeChanged, CardDueDateChanged, CardPriorityChanged.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>List structural changes (STORY-6.3).</li><li>Comment changes (STORY-6.4).</li><li>Presence (STORY-6.5).</li><li>Optimistic UI updates on the originating client (those are handled by the Pinia store write in the mutation path, not by SignalR).</li><li>Conflict UI beyond last-write-wins.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.2, §2.4, §2.9</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> Member A and Member B are both viewing board X (both in group board-{X}) <b>When</b> Member A creates a card <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B's board view adds the card to the correct list in the correct position without a page reload; Member A's own view is not double-updated (the mutation already applied locally). The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A is in the board group and performs a mutation <b>When</b> their own broadcast event is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA store update is idempotent — no duplicate card, list, or comment appears as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A edits a card's title <b>When</b> the change is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated title on the card.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A moves a card from List A to List B <b>When</b> the move is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the card removed from List A and appear in List B at the correct position.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A reorders cards within a list <b>When</b> the new positions are persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B's list reflects the new order.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A deletes a card <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B's view removes that card from the list with no error state.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A updates a card's metadata (label, assignee, due date, or priority — EPIC-4) <b>When</b> the change is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated metadata on the card.</p><p><b>Given</b> the propagated event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect retrieves all changes missed during the outage; no real-time messages are lost or cause stale state.</p><p><b>Given</b> a card mutation event arrives for a board the client has left <b>When</b> the SPA receives it <b>Then</b> it is silently ignored (no stale state, no error).</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-6.2: Propagate card mutations to board group in real time" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-6; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As a board member viewing a board, I want card changes made by other members (create, edit, move between lists, reorder, delete, and metadata updates) to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that I always see the current state of the board without manual intervention.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): from the moment the API persists the mutation to the moment the SignalR message is delivered to connected clients. The broadcast is issued by the Application layer (via IBoardEventPublisher) within the same request after the DB write commits; no async queue introduces extra latency.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): broadcast is addressed to group board-{boardId} via the Azure SignalR Service; any API instance can issue it; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): the IBoardEventPublisher interface lives in Application; its SignalR implementation lives in Infrastructure (IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;); command handlers call the publisher — no hub-to-handler dependency inversion.</li><li>Hub authorization (§EPIC-6 spine): only members of the board receive messages in board-{boardId}; server-side group membership (STORY-6.1) enforces this. No client-side filtering needed.</li><li>Message shape: each event carries a typed, versioned DTO (e.g. CardCreatedEvent, CardMovedEvent, CardDeletedEvent, CardMetadataUpdatedEvent). DTOs are defined in Application and serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency / last-write-wins: no OT or CRDT; the last persisted write wins. The SPA applies each incoming event to the Pinia store immutably (replace-in-place by id); stale events for deleted cards are silently dropped.</li><li>No self-echo: the broadcaster does not need to suppress delivery to the originating connection (Azure SignalR handles broadcasting to the group; if the originating client is in the group it will receive the event — the SPA store update must be idempotent to handle this).</li><li>Security / authorization: the publish call is inside the command handler, which already enforces role-based authorization (STORY-1.5); no additional auth on the publish path.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live card additions/removals/updates do not steal keyboard focus; an aria-live='polite' region announces significant changes (e.g. 'Card 'Deploy infra' moved to Done').</li><li>Card metadata fields propagated: label assignments, assignee, due date, priority (all EPIC-4 mutations). The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A is in the board group and performs a mutation <b>When</b> their own broadcast event is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA store update is idempotent — no duplicate card, list, or comment appears as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A edits a card's title <b>When</b> the change is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated title on the card.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A moves a card from List A to List B <b>When</b> the move is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the card removed from List A and appear in List B at the correct position.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A reorders cards within a list <b>When</b> the new positions are persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B's list reflects the new order.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A deletes a card <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B's view removes that card from the list with no error state.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A updates a card's metadata (label, assignee, due date, or priority — EPIC-4) <b>When</b> the change is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated metadata on the card.</p><p><b>Given</b> the propagated event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect retrieves all changes missed during the outage; no real-time messages are lost or cause stale state.</p><p><b>Given</b> a card mutation event arrives for a board the client has left <b>When</b> the SPA receives it <b>Then</b> it is silently ignored (no stale state, no error).</p>"

### User Story — STORY-6.3: Propagate list and board structural changes to board group in real time
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-6 → <EPIC-6-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-6; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As a board member viewing a board, I want list mutations (create, rename, delete, reorder) and board-level structural changes (board rename, member added/role changed/removed) to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that the board structure I see is always current.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): broadcast issued via IBoardEventPublisher within the same request after the DB write commits.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): group board-{boardId} broadcast; any API instance can publish; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): IBoardEventPublisher interface in Application; SignalR implementation in Infrastructure via IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;; command handlers call the publisher post-commit.</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): group membership (STORY-6.1) ensures only board members receive events. Server-side; client cannot bypass.</li><li>Removed-member handling: the Infrastructure IBoardEventPublisher implementation (which holds IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;) calls Groups.RemoveFromGroupAsync for every connection belonging to the removed user immediately after broadcasting BoardMemberRemovedEvent to the group. The Application layer has no knowledge of connection ids — the eviction call lives entirely in the Infrastructure publisher. After eviction the removed user may no longer receive events for that board.</li><li>Message shape: typed event DTOs (e.g. ListCreatedEvent, ListRenamedEvent, ListDeletedEvent, ListsReorderedEvent, BoardRenamedEvent, BoardMemberAddedEvent, BoardMemberRoleChangedEvent, BoardMemberRemovedEvent) serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency / last-write-wins: Pinia store applies events immutably (replace/add/remove by id); stale events for deleted lists or removed members are silently dropped.</li><li>Role-change client effect: BoardMemberRoleChangedEvent carries the new role; Pinia board store updates the local user's myRole if the event targets the current user. The UI re-evaluates button/action visibility reactively.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live list additions/removals and board-name updates do not steal focus; an aria-live='polite' region announces changes; the 'removed from board' toast is announced via role='alert'.</li><li>Security: publish call is inside the already-authorized command handler (STORY-1.5 role matrix); no extra auth on the publish path.</li><li>Group-eviction call site (Clean Architecture): Groups.RemoveFromGroupAsync MUST be called from the Infrastructure IBoardEventPublisher implementation, not from any Application layer class. The Application layer issues no SignalR calls and holds no reference to IHubContext or connection ids.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Card mutations (STORY-6.2).</li><li>Comment mutations (STORY-6.4).</li><li>Presence (STORY-6.5).</li><li>Pushing the removed member's browser to a login page (navigate-to-board-list is sufficient).</li><li>Real-time propagation of board deletion (edge case: if the board is deleted, members still viewing it will see a REST error on the next interaction and navigate away).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.2, §2.4, §2.9</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> Member A and Member B are both viewing board X <b>When</b> Member A creates a new list <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the new list column appears in Member B's board view at the correct position. The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A is in the board group and performs a list or board structural mutation <b>When</b> their own broadcast event is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA store update is idempotent — no duplicate list, member entry, or board name update appears as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A renames a list <b>When</b> the rename is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list header updates in Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A deletes a list (and its cards cascade) <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list column and all its cards disappear from Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A reorders lists <b>When</b> the new positions are persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list order reflects the change in Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner renames the board <b>When</b> the rename is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated board name in the board header and browser tab title.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner adds a new member (EPIC-1 STORY-1.2) <b>When</b> the add is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s all existing connected members see the updated member count/list (if the members panel is open). The newly added member is not yet in the SignalR group — they must open the board and call JoinBoard (STORY-6.1) to start receiving updates.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner changes a member's role (EPIC-1 STORY-1.3) <b>When</b> the change is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s existing connected members (including the affected member) receive a BoardMemberRoleChanged event; the affected member's local permissions are refreshed from the store (UI re-evaluates which actions are available to them).</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner removes a member (EPIC-1 STORY-1.4) <b>When</b> the removal is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the removed member receives a BoardMemberRemoved event targeted at their user (or broadcast to the group before the hub removes them from the group); the removed member's SPA navigates to the board list with a 'You have been removed from this board' toast; other connected members see the membership update.</p><p><b>Given</b> the propagated event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect retrieves all changes missed during the outage.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-6.3: Propagate list and board structural changes to board group in real time" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-6; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As a board member viewing a board, I want list mutations (create, rename, delete, reorder) and board-level structural changes (board rename, member added/role changed/removed) to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that the board structure I see is always current.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): broadcast issued via IBoardEventPublisher within the same request after the DB write commits.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): group board-{boardId} broadcast; any API instance can publish; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): IBoardEventPublisher interface in Application; SignalR implementation in Infrastructure via IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;; command handlers call the publisher post-commit.</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): group membership (STORY-6.1) ensures only board members receive events. Server-side; client cannot bypass.</li><li>Removed-member handling: the Infrastructure IBoardEventPublisher implementation (which holds IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;) calls Groups.RemoveFromGroupAsync for every connection belonging to the removed user immediately after broadcasting BoardMemberRemovedEvent to the group. The Application layer has no knowledge of connection ids — the eviction call lives entirely in the Infrastructure publisher. After eviction the removed user may no longer receive events for that board.</li><li>Message shape: typed event DTOs (e.g. ListCreatedEvent, ListRenamedEvent, ListDeletedEvent, ListsReorderedEvent, BoardRenamedEvent, BoardMemberAddedEvent, BoardMemberRoleChangedEvent, BoardMemberRemovedEvent) serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency / last-write-wins: Pinia store applies events immutably (replace/add/remove by id); stale events for deleted lists or removed members are silently dropped.</li><li>Role-change client effect: BoardMemberRoleChangedEvent carries the new role; Pinia board store updates the local user's myRole if the event targets the current user. The UI re-evaluates button/action visibility reactively.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live list additions/removals and board-name updates do not steal focus; an aria-live='polite' region announces changes; the 'removed from board' toast is announced via role='alert'.</li><li>Security: publish call is inside the already-authorized command handler (STORY-1.5 role matrix); no extra auth on the publish path.</li><li>Group-eviction call site (Clean Architecture): Groups.RemoveFromGroupAsync MUST be called from the Infrastructure IBoardEventPublisher implementation, not from any Application layer class. The Application layer issues no SignalR calls and holds no reference to IHubContext or connection ids.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Card mutations (STORY-6.2).</li><li>Comment mutations (STORY-6.4).</li><li>Presence (STORY-6.5).</li><li>Pushing the removed member's browser to a login page (navigate-to-board-list is sufficient).</li><li>Real-time propagation of board deletion (edge case: if the board is deleted, members still viewing it will see a REST error on the next interaction and navigate away).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.2, §2.4, §2.9</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> Member A and Member B are both viewing board X <b>When</b> Member A creates a new list <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the new list column appears in Member B's board view at the correct position. The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A is in the board group and performs a list or board structural mutation <b>When</b> their own broadcast event is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA store update is idempotent — no duplicate list, member entry, or board name update appears as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A renames a list <b>When</b> the rename is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list header updates in Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A deletes a list (and its cards cascade) <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list column and all its cards disappear from Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A reorders lists <b>When</b> the new positions are persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the list order reflects the change in Member B's view.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner renames the board <b>When</b> the rename is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated board name in the board header and browser tab title.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner adds a new member (EPIC-1 STORY-1.2) <b>When</b> the add is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s all existing connected members see the updated member count/list (if the members panel is open). The newly added member is not yet in the SignalR group — they must open the board and call JoinBoard (STORY-6.1) to start receiving updates.</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner changes a member's role (EPIC-1 STORY-1.3) <b>When</b> the change is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s existing connected members (including the affected member) receive a BoardMemberRoleChanged event; the affected member's local permissions are refreshed from the store (UI re-evaluates which actions are available to them).</p><p><b>Given</b> the board Owner removes a member (EPIC-1 STORY-1.4) <b>When</b> the removal is persisted <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the removed member receives a BoardMemberRemoved event targeted at their user (or broadcast to the group before the hub removes them from the group); the removed member's SPA navigates to the board list with a 'You have been removed from this board' toast; other connected members see the membership update.</p><p><b>Given</b> the propagated event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect retrieves all changes missed during the outage.</p>"

### User Story — STORY-6.4: Propagate comment mutations to board group in real time
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-6 → <EPIC-6-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-6; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As a board member viewing a card's comment thread, I want new, edited, and deleted comments to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that I can follow the discussion without polling or reloading.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): broadcast issued via IBoardEventPublisher within the same request after the DB write commits; no async queue.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): broadcast to group board-{boardId} via the Azure SignalR Service; any API instance may publish; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): IBoardEventPublisher interface in Application; SignalR implementation in Infrastructure via IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;; EPIC-5 comment command handlers call the publisher after committing the mutation.</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): group board-{boardId} (STORY-6.1) ensures only board members receive comment events. Server-side.</li><li>Message shape: typed event DTOs — CommentAddedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId, authorId, authorDisplayName, body, createdAt), CommentEditedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId, body, editedAt), CommentDeletedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId). DTOs serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency: Pinia comment store applies events immutably (add/replace/remove by commentId); duplicate events (e.g. self-echo) are idempotent; events for unknown commentIds on delete are silently dropped.</li><li>No self-echo suppression required: if the originating client receives its own event, the store update is idempotent.</li><li>Pagination consistency: comments are paginated (EPIC-5 STORY-5.2); incoming CommentAddedEvent appends the comment to the currently loaded page if the thread is visible; it does not reload the full paginated list.</li><li>Security: publish call is inside the already-authorized EPIC-5 command handler (STORY-1.5 role matrix); no extra auth on the publish path.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live comment additions use aria-live='polite' in the comment thread container; deletions do not orphan keyboard focus; no color-only change signals.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Card mutations (STORY-6.2).</li><li>List and board structural changes (STORY-6.3).</li><li>Presence (STORY-6.5).</li><li>Notifications when the user is not viewing the board.</li><li>Typing indicators ('Member A is typing...').</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.5, §1.6, §2.2, §2.4, §2.9</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> Member A and Member B are both viewing board X, and Member B has the comment thread of card C open <b>When</b> Member A posts a new comment on card C <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the new comment appears at the bottom of Member B's comment thread without a page reload. The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> the originating member (Member A) is in the board group <b>When</b> their own CommentAddedEvent, CommentEditedEvent, or CommentDeletedEvent is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA comment store update is idempotent — no duplicate comment appears and no existing comment is doubly removed as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A edits their own comment <b>When</b> the edit is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated comment body and the '(edited)' indicator on that comment.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A (or the board Owner) deletes a comment <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the comment disappears from Member B's thread; if Member B had that comment focused, focus moves to the next logical element (keyboard accessibility).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B has the card's comment thread closed (or the card detail is not open) <b>When</b> a comment event arrives <b>Then</b> the Pinia comment store is updated silently; when Member B opens the thread they see the current state without a separate fetch.</p><p><b>Given</b> the event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect includes an up-to-date comment count; Member B fetches the comment thread on demand and sees current comments (no special comment replay needed).</p><p><b>Given</b> a comment event arrives for a card that belongs to a different board than board-{X} <b>When</b> the SPA receives it <b>Then</b> it is silently ignored (no stale state, no error).</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-6.4: Propagate comment mutations to board group in real time" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-6; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As a board member viewing a card's comment thread, I want new, edited, and deleted comments to appear in my view within ~1 s with no refresh, so that I can follow the discussion without polling or reloading.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>&lt; ~1 s propagation (§1.6): broadcast issued via IBoardEventPublisher within the same request after the DB write commits; no async queue.</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): broadcast to group board-{boardId} via the Azure SignalR Service; any API instance may publish; no per-instance socket state.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): IBoardEventPublisher interface in Application; SignalR implementation in Infrastructure via IHubContext&lt;BoardHub&gt;; EPIC-5 comment command handlers call the publisher after committing the mutation.</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): group board-{boardId} (STORY-6.1) ensures only board members receive comment events. Server-side.</li><li>Message shape: typed event DTOs — CommentAddedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId, authorId, authorDisplayName, body, createdAt), CommentEditedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId, body, editedAt), CommentDeletedEvent (commentId, cardId, boardId). DTOs serialized as camelCase JSON. No raw DB entities over the wire.</li><li>Idempotency: Pinia comment store applies events immutably (add/replace/remove by commentId); duplicate events (e.g. self-echo) are idempotent; events for unknown commentIds on delete are silently dropped.</li><li>No self-echo suppression required: if the originating client receives its own event, the store update is idempotent.</li><li>Pagination consistency: comments are paginated (EPIC-5 STORY-5.2); incoming CommentAddedEvent appends the comment to the currently loaded page if the thread is visible; it does not reload the full paginated list.</li><li>Security: publish call is inside the already-authorized EPIC-5 command handler (STORY-1.5 role matrix); no extra auth on the publish path.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: live comment additions use aria-live='polite' in the comment thread container; deletions do not orphan keyboard focus; no color-only change signals.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Card mutations (STORY-6.2).</li><li>List and board structural changes (STORY-6.3).</li><li>Presence (STORY-6.5).</li><li>Notifications when the user is not viewing the board.</li><li>Typing indicators ('Member A is typing...').</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.5, §1.6, §2.2, §2.4, §2.9</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> Member A and Member B are both viewing board X, and Member B has the comment thread of card C open <b>When</b> Member A posts a new comment on card C <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the new comment appears at the bottom of Member B's comment thread without a page reload. The two-client integration test asserts that the receiver observes the event within a <b>2 s CI wall-clock timeout</b> (validating the &lt;1 s NFR with headroom for CI overhead).</p><p><b>Given</b> the originating member (Member A) is in the board group <b>When</b> their own CommentAddedEvent, CommentEditedEvent, or CommentDeletedEvent is delivered back to their connection <b>Then</b> the SPA comment store update is idempotent — no duplicate comment appears and no existing comment is doubly removed as a result of the self-echo.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A edits their own comment <b>When</b> the edit is saved <b>Then</b> within ~1 s Member B sees the updated comment body and the '(edited)' indicator on that comment.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member A (or the board Owner) deletes a comment <b>When</b> the deletion is committed <b>Then</b> within ~1 s the comment disappears from Member B's thread; if Member B had that comment focused, focus moves to the next logical element (keyboard accessibility).</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B has the card's comment thread closed (or the card detail is not open) <b>When</b> a comment event arrives <b>Then</b> the Pinia comment store is updated silently; when Member B opens the thread they see the current state without a separate fetch.</p><p><b>Given</b> the event arrives while Member B is offline or reconnecting <b>When</b> Member B reconnects (per STORY-6.1) <b>Then</b> the full-board reload on reconnect includes an up-to-date comment count; Member B fetches the comment thread on demand and sees current comments (no special comment replay needed).</p><p><b>Given</b> a comment event arrives for a card that belongs to a different board than board-{X} <b>When</b> the SPA receives it <b>Then</b> it is silently ignored (no stale state, no error).</p>"

### User Story — STORY-6.5: Presence — show which members are currently viewing the board (optional)
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-6 → <EPIC-6-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-6; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As a board member, I want to see avatar indicators for other members who are currently viewing the same board, so that I know when I am collaborating in real time and can expect to see their changes appear live.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Best-effort, event-driven only: presence state is accumulated on each client from MemberJoinedPresence and MemberLeftPresence events. There is no server-generated authoritative snapshot. The SPA initialises its own presence entry on JoinBoard success; it does not rely on a server-side group enumeration.</li><li>No BoardPresenceSnapshot: the hub does NOT send a snapshot of currently connected members on join. Azure SignalR Default mode provides no group-membership enumeration API. Any implementation that calls such an API is a bug.</li><li>Future upgrade path (out of scope): a Redis-backed IPresenceStore behind the existing ICacheService seam would enable the hub to emit a BoardPresenceSnapshot on JoinBoard. This is deferred until a paid tier with Redis is available.</li><li>Best-effort latency: presence join broadcast is &lt; ~1 s; graceful leave broadcast is &lt; ~1 s; ungraceful-disconnect leave is &lt; ~5 s (bounded by SignalR keep-alive timeout).</li><li>Azure SignalR Default mode / scale-out safety (§2.4, §2.9): MemberJoinedPresence / MemberLeftPresence are broadcast to group board-{boardId} from the hub layer; no per-instance in-memory presence list.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): presence events are broadcast directly from the hub (BoardHub) — presence is a connection concern, not a domain mutation. This is the one case where the hub directly sends a group message without going through the Application layer.</li><li>Hub authorization (EPIC-6 spine): JoinBoard already validates board membership (STORY-6.1); presence broadcast piggybacks on that — no separate auth step.</li><li>Message shape: MemberJoinedPresence DTO (userId, displayName, avatarUrl, boardId) and MemberLeftPresence DTO (userId, boardId). Serialized as camelCase JSON.</li><li>SPA presence store: a presenceStore (Pinia) holds a Map&lt;boardId, Set&lt;UserPresence&gt;&gt;. On JoinBoard success the SPA adds its own entry immediately. MemberJoinedPresence adds; MemberLeftPresence removes. Duplicate MemberJoinedPresence for the same userId is idempotent (no double avatar). On reconnect, the SPA clears its local set and re-adds itself, then accumulates new events (no snapshot to rebuild from).</li><li>No persistence: presence is ephemeral; no DB writes; no history.</li><li>Privacy: only board members may see the presence bar (enforced via group membership — only board members are in board-{boardId}). No leaking to non-members.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: avatar images have alt text (member display name); overflow popover is keyboard-reachable (role='tooltip' or disclosure button); presence bar does not steal focus; aria-live='polite' announces join/leave to screen readers (e.g. 'Alex joined the board').</li></ul><p><b>Known limitation:</b> a late-joiner accumulates presence only from MemberJoinedPresence / MemberLeftPresence events that arrive after it connects. Members who were already viewing the board before the late-joiner connected are not visible until they perform another action that re-broadcasts their presence (e.g. a future heartbeat, out of scope now). This is the accepted trade-off of best-effort event-driven presence without a Redis-backed snapshot.</p><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Per-card presence ('Member A is editing this card').</li><li>Typing indicators in comment threads.</li><li>Presence history or 'last seen' timestamps.</li><li>Presence outside the current board view (global 'who's online').</li><li>Push notifications triggered by presence.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.4, §2.9</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> Member A is viewing board X <b>When</b> Member B opens board X and the hub calls JoinBoard <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts a MemberJoinedPresence event (userId, displayName, avatarUrl, boardId) to the board-{X} group; within ~1 s Member A's SPA receives the event and adds Member B's avatar to the presence bar.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B navigates away from board X and the SPA calls LeaveBoard(boardId) <b>When</b> the hub receives the call <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts a MemberLeftPresence event (userId, boardId) to the board-{X} group; within ~1 s Member A's presence bar removes Member B's avatar. (Best-effort: this requires a clean LeaveBoard call.)</p><p><b>Given</b> a member's connection drops ungracefully (network failure, not a clean LeaveBoard) <b>When</b> the SignalR keep-alive times out and OnDisconnectedAsync fires <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts MemberLeftPresence for that user; Member A's presence bar removes the departed avatar within ~5 s of the timeout.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B reconnects after a drop <b>When</b> JoinBoard is called again (per STORY-6.1 reconnect logic) <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts MemberJoinedPresence again and Member B reappears in Member A's presence bar.</p><p><b>Given</b> multiple members are viewing the board <b>When</b> there are more than N avatars (configurable, default 5) <b>Then</b> the presence bar shows N avatars plus a '+K others' overflow indicator; all members are listed in an accessible tooltip/popover on that indicator.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am viewing my own avatar in the presence bar <b>When</b> I inspect the presence bar <b>Then</b> my own avatar is visually distinguished (e.g. 'You' label, ring) so I can distinguish myself from others; my avatar is always shown (the SPA adds itself on JoinBoard success without waiting for a server echo).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am a Viewer <b>When</b> I view the presence bar <b>Then</b> I see all members who have announced themselves after I joined; presence is a read-only feature available to all roles.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-6.5: Presence — show which members are currently viewing the board (optional)" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-6; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As a board member, I want to see avatar indicators for other members who are currently viewing the same board, so that I know when I am collaborating in real time and can expect to see their changes appear live.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Best-effort, event-driven only: presence state is accumulated on each client from MemberJoinedPresence and MemberLeftPresence events. There is no server-generated authoritative snapshot. Serialized as camelCase JSON.</li><li>SPA presence store: a presenceStore (Pinia) holds a Map&lt;boardId, Set&lt;UserPresence&gt;&gt;. On JoinBoard success the SPA adds its own entry immediately. MemberJoinedPresence adds; MemberLeftPresence removes. Duplicate MemberJoinedPresence for the same userId is idempotent (no double avatar). No leaking to non-members.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA: avatar images have alt text (member display name); overflow popover is keyboard-reachable (role='tooltip' or disclosure button); presence bar does not steal focus; aria-live='polite' announces join/leave to screen readers (e.g. 'Alex joined the board').</li></ul><p><b>Known limitation:</b> a late-joiner accumulates presence only from MemberJoinedPresence / MemberLeftPresence events that arrive after it connects. Members who were already viewing the board before the late-joiner connected are not visible until they perform another action that re-broadcasts their presence (e.g. a future heartbeat, out of scope now). This is the accepted trade-off of best-effort event-driven presence without a Redis-backed snapshot.</p><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Per-card presence ('Member A is editing this card').</li><li>Typing indicators in comment threads.</li><li>Presence history or 'last seen' timestamps.</li><li>Presence outside the current board view (global 'who's online').</li><li>Push notifications triggered by presence.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.2, §1.5, §1.6, §2.4, §2.9</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> Member A is viewing board X <b>When</b> Member B opens board X and the hub calls JoinBoard <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts a MemberJoinedPresence event (userId, displayName, avatarUrl, boardId) to the board-{X} group; within ~1 s Member A's SPA receives the event and adds Member B's avatar to the presence bar.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B navigates away from board X and the SPA calls LeaveBoard(boardId) <b>When</b> the hub receives the call <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts a MemberLeftPresence event (userId, boardId) to the board-{X} group; within ~1 s Member A's presence bar removes Member B's avatar. (Best-effort: this requires a clean LeaveBoard call.)</p><p><b>Given</b> a member's connection drops ungracefully (network failure, not a clean LeaveBoard) <b>When</b> the SignalR keep-alive times out and OnDisconnectedAsync fires <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts MemberLeftPresence for that user; Member A's presence bar removes the departed avatar within ~5 s of the timeout.</p><p><b>Given</b> Member B reconnects after a drop <b>When</b> JoinBoard is called again (per STORY-6.1 reconnect logic) <b>Then</b> the hub broadcasts MemberJoinedPresence again and Member B reappears in Member A's presence bar.</p><p><b>Given</b> multiple members are viewing the board <b>When</b> there are more than N avatars (configurable, default 5) <b>Then</b> the presence bar shows N avatars plus a '+K others' overflow indicator; all members are listed in an accessible tooltip/popover on that indicator.</p><p><b>Given</b> I am viewing my own avatar in the presence bar <b>When</b> I inspect the presence bar <b>Then</b> my own avatar is visually distinguished (e.g. 'You' label, ring) so I can distinguish myself from others; my avatar is always shown (the SPA adds itself on JoinBoard success without waiting for a server echo).</p><p><b>Given</b> I am a Viewer <b>When</b> I view the presence bar <b>Then</b> I see all members who have announced themselves after I joined; presence is a read-only feature available to all roles.</p>"
```

**Link to parent**
```
az boards work-item relation add --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --id <this-story-id> --relation-type parent --target-id <EPIC-6-id>
```

---

### User Story — STORY-7.1: Record activity events
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-7 → <EPIC-7-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-7; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As the system, I want to append an immutable activity entry to a board's log whenever a member performs a mutation, so that the board's history is always accurate and in sync with reality.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Atomicity: the activity entry MUST be written in the same EF Core SaveChanges call (same unit of work / database transaction) as the mutation it records. The feed must never drift from the actual state of the board.</li><li>Immutability: ActivityEntry rows have no update or delete paths in the application layer. No endpoint, background job, or migration may mutate existing rows. The EF entity has no setter for any field beyond the constructor.</li><li>Snapshot preservation: actor display name and target label (e.g. card title, list name) are captured at write time so the entry remains meaningful if the source entity is later renamed or deleted.</li><li>Clean Architecture (§2.2): ActivityEntry entity lives in Domain; IActivityWriter interface (or equivalent domain event / outbox pattern) lives in Application; the EF Core ActivityEntries table and write implementation live in Infrastructure. No EF or Microsoft.* namespace references in Domain.</li><li>No circular dependency: mutation use-cases (EPIC-2 through EPIC-5) dispatch domain events or call IActivityWriter; the activity infrastructure handles persistence. Mutation handlers must not directly construct ActivityEntry rows with EF types.</li><li>Security / authorization: the writer is called only from within authenticated, authorized use-cases — it trusts the actorId it is given and does not re-authorize.</li><li>RFC 7807 / DTOs: no activity DTO is exposed by this story (read path is STORY-7.2). This story only concerns the write path.</li><li>Performance: writing an entry must not add a perceptible round-trip; it is part of the same transaction as the mutation.</li><li>EF migration: an ActivityEntries table is created by a new EF Core migration with columns: Id (PK, Guid), BoardId (FK), ActorId (FK → Users), ActorDisplayName (string, snapshot), EventType (string), Description (string), OccurredAt (DateTimeOffset UTC). Index on (BoardId, OccurredAt DESC) to support the read path efficiently.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Comment edits producing an activity entry (comment editing is out of v1.0 scope).</li><li>System-generated or automated entries with no human actor.</li><li>Activity for board creation or deletion (board creation is covered by EPIC-0/EPIC-1; board deletion is a separate story).</li><li>The read (feed) endpoint — that is STORY-7.2.</li><li>Real-time push of new entries to open clients — that is STORY-7.3.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.3, §1.5, §2.2</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully creates, updates, or deletes a list on the board <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written in the same database transaction, recording: boardId, actorId, actor display name (snapshot), eventType, target entity id, a human-readable description snapshot (e.g. 'List 'Backlog' created'), and occurredAt (UTC). The entry is visible in subsequent feed reads.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully creates, updates (title, description, due date, priority, position/list), reorders within a list, or deletes a card <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written in the same transaction with eventType from the card event types below and a snapshot description (e.g. 'Card 'Fix login bug' moved to 'In Progress'' or 'Card 'Fix login bug' repositioned in 'In Progress''). The entry persists even if the card is later deleted.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully reorders lists on the board <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written in the same transaction with eventType: list.reordered and a snapshot description (e.g. 'Lists reordered'). The entry is visible in subsequent feed reads.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully adds or removes a label from a card, or creates/renames/deletes a board-level label <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with the appropriate eventType and description snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully assigns or unassigns a member from a card <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written recording the assignee's display name snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully creates or deletes a comment on a card <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written recording the comment's card title snapshot. (Comment edits are out of scope — see Out of scope.)</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner adds or removes a board member or changes a member's role <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with the affected member's display name snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner renames the board itself <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with eventType: board.renamed and snapshots of the old and new name.</p><p><b>Given</b> any mutation that would normally produce an activity entry fails (e.g. a validation error or a rollback) <b>Then</b> no activity entry is written (transactional atomicity guaranteed — the log cannot drift from reality).</p><p><b>Given</b> a Viewer attempts any mutation endpoint <b>When</b> the request is processed <b>Then</b> the mutation is rejected (the mutation story's own auth enforces this) and therefore no activity entry is written — entry creation is strictly a side effect of successful commits.</p>
```

**Create**
```

The entry persists even if the card is later deleted.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully reorders lists on the board <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written in the same transaction with eventType: list.reordered and a snapshot description (e.g. 'Lists reordered'). The entry is visible in subsequent feed reads.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully adds or removes a label from a card, or creates/renames/deletes a board-level label <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with the appropriate eventType and description snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully assigns or unassigns a member from a card <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written recording the assignee's display name snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner or Editor successfully creates or deletes a comment on a card <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written recording the comment's card title snapshot. (Comment edits are out of scope — see Out of scope.)</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner adds or removes a board member or changes a member's role <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with the affected member's display name snapshot.</p><p><b>Given</b> a board Owner renames the board itself <b>When</b> the mutation commits <b>Then</b> an activity entry is written with eventType: board.renamed and snapshots of the old and new name.</p><p><b>Given</b> any mutation that would normally produce an activity entry fails (e.g. a validation error or a rollback) <b>Then</b> no activity entry is written (transactional atomicity guaranteed — the log cannot drift from reality).</p><p><b>Given</b> a Viewer attempts any mutation endpoint <b>When</b> the request is processed <b>Then</b> the mutation is rejected (the mutation story's own auth enforces this) and therefore no activity entry is written — entry creation is strictly a side effect of successful commits.</p>"
