### User Story — STORY-10.1: Liveness & readiness health probes
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-10 → <EPIC-10-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-10; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As an on-call engineer (or load-balancer orchestrator), I want the API to expose a DB-free liveness probe and a SQL-checking readiness probe, so that the platform can distinguish 'process is up' from 'process can serve traffic' without requiring authentication.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Both endpoints are UNAUTHENTICATED — no [Authorize] attribute, no JWT middleware applied to these routes.</li><li>/health must be DB-free — no EF Core call, no SQL ping, no infrastructure dependency beyond process health.</li><li>/health/ready SQL check uses ASP.NET Core's built-in Microsoft.Extensions.Diagnostics.HealthChecks with AddSqlServer (or equivalent EF Core check) — no custom polling loop.</li><li>Health-check responses must never include connection strings, credentials, or internal stack traces.</li><li>Both endpoints must respond in isolation (before middleware that would add auth, before SignalR negotiation, etc.); register them before app.UseAuthentication() in the pipeline ordering.</li><li>Timeout for the SQL check: configurable, default 5 s; the probe returns 503 on timeout, not an unhandled exception.</li><li>Clean Architecture: health-check registration lives in the Infrastructure project (SQL probe) and the Api project (endpoint mapping); no reference to Microsoft.Extensions.Diagnostics.HealthChecks from Domain or Application.</li><li>Pipeline order (shared constraint — identical in STORY-10.2): the concrete middleware registration order in Program.cs MUST be: (1) exception-handling middleware (UseExceptionHandler / global error handler from STORY-10.2) registered FIRST as the outermost layer; (2) correlation-id middleware (STORY-10.3) registered second; (3) health endpoints (MapHealthChecks) mapped next — they resolve before authentication so they are always reachable; (4) UseRouting; (5) UseAuthentication / UseAuthorization. The health endpoints bypass auth because they are mapped before UseAuthentication. The error handler wraps everything including health checks.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Deep health checks for SignalR, Key Vault, or Sentry (those surface via their own SDK exceptions and Sentry captures).</li><li>A UI health dashboard or status page exposed to end-users.</li><li>Custom health-check serialization beyond ASP.NET Core's default HealthStatus JSON writer (unless HealthCheckOptions.ResponseWriter is needed to strip secrets — then only that).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §2.9, §1.6</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> the API process is running <b>When</b> anything (load balancer, monitoring tool, or operator) sends GET /health <b>Then</b> the response is 200 OK with Content-Type: application/json body {'status':'Healthy'} — with no database call made, no authentication required, and the response time under 100 ms in any environment.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API process is running and SQL Server is reachable <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called <b>Then</b> the response is 200 OK with body {'status':'Healthy','checks':[{'name':'sqlserver','status':'Healthy'}]} (or equivalent structured shape) and no authentication is required.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API process is running but SQL Server is unreachable (network partition, SQL paused) <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called <b>Then</b> the response is 503 Service Unavailable with body {'status':'Unhealthy','checks':[{'name':'sqlserver','status':'Unhealthy','description':'&lt;non-sensitive error summary&gt;'}]} — no stack trace or connection-string value is included in the response body.</p><p><b>Given</b> SQL recovers after a readiness failure <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called again <b>Then</b> it returns 200 OK (the check is live, not latched).</p><p><b>Given</b> either probe is called <b>When</b> the response is returned <b>Then</b> it includes a X-Correlation-Id header (consistent with STORY-10.3) even though no authentication is required.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-10.1: Liveness & readiness health probes" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-10; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As an on-call engineer (or load-balancer orchestrator), I want the API to expose a DB-free liveness probe and a SQL-checking readiness probe, so that the platform can distinguish 'process is up' from 'process can serve traffic' without requiring authentication.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Both endpoints are UNAUTHENTICATED — no [Authorize] attribute, no JWT middleware applied to these routes.</li><li>/health must be DB-free — no EF Core call, no SQL ping, no infrastructure dependency beyond process health.</li><li>/health/ready SQL check uses ASP.NET Core's built-in Microsoft.Extensions.Diagnostics.HealthChecks with AddSqlServer (or equivalent EF Core check) — no custom polling loop.</li><li>Health-check responses must never include connection strings, credentials, or internal stack traces.</li><li>Both endpoints must respond in isolation (before middleware that would add auth, before SignalR negotiation, etc.); register them before app.UseAuthentication() in the pipeline ordering.</li><li>Timeout for the SQL check: configurable, default 5 s; the probe returns 503 on timeout, not an unhandled exception.</li><li>Clean Architecture: health-check registration lives in the Infrastructure project (SQL probe) and the Api project (endpoint mapping); no reference to Microsoft.Extensions.Diagnostics.HealthChecks from Domain or Application.</li><li>Pipeline order (shared constraint — identical in STORY-10.2): the concrete middleware registration order in Program.cs MUST be: (1) exception-handling middleware (UseExceptionHandler / global error handler from STORY-10.2) registered FIRST as the outermost layer; (2) correlation-id middleware (STORY-10.3) registered second; (3) health endpoints (MapHealthChecks) mapped next — they resolve before authentication so they are always reachable; (4) UseRouting; (5) UseAuthentication / UseAuthorization. The health endpoints bypass auth because they are mapped before UseAuthentication. The error handler wraps everything including health checks.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Deep health checks for SignalR, Key Vault, or Sentry (those surface via their own SDK exceptions and Sentry captures).</li><li>A UI health dashboard or status page exposed to end-users.</li><li>Custom health-check serialization beyond ASP.NET Core's default HealthStatus JSON writer (unless HealthCheckOptions.ResponseWriter is needed to strip secrets — then only that).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §2.9, §1.6</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> the API process is running <b>When</b> anything (load balancer, monitoring tool, or operator) sends GET /health <b>Then</b> the response is 200 OK with Content-Type: application/json body {'status':'Healthy'} — with no database call made, no authentication required, and the response time under 100 ms in any environment.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API process is running and SQL Server is reachable <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called <b>Then</b> the response is 200 OK with body {'status':'Healthy','checks':[{'name':'sqlserver','status':'Healthy'}]} (or equivalent structured shape) and no authentication is required.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API process is running but SQL Server is unreachable (network partition, SQL paused) <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called <b>Then</b> the response is 503 Service Unavailable with body {'status':'Unhealthy','checks':[{'name':'sqlserver','status':'Unhealthy','description':'&lt;non-sensitive error summary&gt;'}]} — no stack trace or connection-string value is included in the response body.</p><p><b>Given</b> SQL recovers after a readiness failure <b>When</b> GET /health/ready is called again <b>Then</b> it returns 200 OK (the check is live, not latched).</p><p><b>Given</b> either probe is called <b>When</b> the response is returned <b>Then</b> it includes a X-Correlation-Id header (consistent with STORY-10.3) even though no authentication is required.</p>"
```

**Link to parent**
```
az boards work-item relation add --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --id <this-story-id> --relation-type parent --target-id <EPIC-10-id>
```

---

### User Story — STORY-10.2: Global error handler → RFC 7807 responses
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-10 → <EPIC-10-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-10; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As an on-call engineer, I want every unhandled exception from the API to produce a structured RFC 7807 problem-details response with a correlation id — and never a raw stack trace or internal detail — so that clients receive consistent, safe error shapes and I can trace any incident back to a specific request.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Implemented as ASP.NET Core middleware (or IExceptionHandler / app.UseExceptionHandler) — a single global registration, not per-controller try/catch blocks.</li><li>The handler must be registered before UseRouting/UseAuthentication in the pipeline so it catches errors from all middleware layers.</li><li>No secrets, PII, or internal stack traces in any response body — ever. The check is mechanical: the serialized response body must not contain the string StackTrace, at System., or the exception's .Message property for unhandled exceptions.</li><li>traceId in the response body and X-Correlation-Id in the response header use the same value (correlation id from STORY-10.3 or HttpContext.TraceIdentifier fallback).</li><li>Validation errors (400) produced by model binding and FluentValidation/DataAnnotations are handled by ASP.NET Core's problem() factory (already RFC 7807-conformant) — the global handler does not need to re-serialize these; it only catches unhandled exceptions (status 500 path).</li><li>Clean Architecture: the error-handler middleware lives in the Api project; it must not import Domain or Application types to produce the response.</li><li>A developer-mode detail extension (detail field showing the exception message) is permissible only when IHostEnvironment.IsDevelopment() is true and must be provably absent in staging/production.</li><li>Pipeline order (shared constraint — identical in STORY-10.1): the concrete middleware registration order in Program.cs MUST be: (1) exception-handling middleware (UseExceptionHandler / global error handler from this story) registered FIRST as the outermost layer; (2) correlation-id middleware (STORY-10.3) registered second; (3) health endpoints (MapHealthChecks) mapped next — they resolve before authentication so they are always reachable; (4) UseRouting; (5) UseAuthentication / UseAuthorization. The health endpoints bypass auth because they are mapped before UseAuthentication. The error handler wraps everything including health checks.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Per-exception mapping to specific 4xx codes (e.g. mapping NotFoundException → 404) — that is domain-error translation handled per-use-case in later epics.</li><li>Sentry capture of errors (STORY-10.4 layers that on top of the structured log entry produced here).</li><li>Retry / circuit-breaker logic (resilience patterns are out of scope for v1.0).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.2</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> any request to the API triggers an unhandled exception (null reference, unexpected domain error, infrastructure failure) <b>When</b> the global error handler catches it <b>Then</b> the response is an RFC 7807 problem-details body (application/problem+json) with at minimum type, title, status, and traceId fields; the status is 500; no stack trace, no exception message, no internal type name, and no PII is included in the response body.</p><p><b>Given</b> the error handler produces a 500 response <b>When</b> the response is serialized <b>Then</b> the traceId field value matches the X-Correlation-Id response header on that same request (set by STORY-10.3's middleware, or a fallback HttpContext.TraceIdentifier if 10.3 is not yet merged).</p><p><b>Given</b> an unhandled exception is caught <b>When</b> the handler logs it <b>Then</b> it logs at Error level with the full exception (message + stack) in the structured log sink, keyed by the same correlation id — the stack trace is in the logs, never in the response.</p><p><b>Given</b> an OperationCanceledException or TaskCanceledException is thrown because the client disconnected <b>When</b> the error handler processes it <b>Then</b> it returns 499 (or swallows cleanly without a 500) and logs at Information or Warning level — not Error.</p><p><b>Given</b> any error response is produced <b>When</b> a client parses it <b>Then</b> the Content-Type is application/problem+json and the body is valid JSON conforming to RFC 7807 (the shape all other epics' error ACs depend on).</p><p><b>Given</b> the API is running normally with no unhandled exceptions <b>When</b> requests succeed <b>Then</b> the error handler adds no observable overhead (it is middleware, not a try/catch on every endpoint).</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-10.2: Global error handler → RFC 7807 responses" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-10; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As an on-call engineer, I want every unhandled exception from the API to produce a structured RFC 7807 problem-details response with a correlation id — and never a raw stack trace or internal detail — so that clients receive consistent, safe error shapes and I can trace any incident back to a specific request.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Implemented as ASP.NET Core middleware (or IExceptionHandler / app.UseExceptionHandler) — a single global registration, not per-controller try/catch blocks.</li><li>The handler must be registered before UseRouting/UseAuthentication in the pipeline so it catches errors from all middleware layers.</li><li>No secrets, PII, or internal stack traces in any response body — ever. The check is mechanical: the serialized response body must not contain the string StackTrace, at System., or the exception's .Message property for unhandled exceptions.</li><li>traceId in the response body and X-Correlation-Id in the response header use the same value (correlation id from STORY-10.3 or HttpContext.TraceIdentifier fallback).</li><li>Validation errors (400) produced by model binding and FluentValidation/DataAnnotations are handled by ASP.NET Core's problem() factory (already RFC 7807-conformant) — the global handler does not need to re-serialize these; it only catches unhandled exceptions (status 500 path).</li><li>Clean Architecture: the error-handler middleware lives in the Api project; it must not import Domain or Application types to produce the response.</li><li>A developer-mode detail extension (detail field showing the exception message) is permissible only when IHostEnvironment.IsDevelopment() is true and must be provably absent in staging/production.</li><li>Pipeline order (shared constraint — identical in STORY-10.1): the concrete middleware registration order in Program.cs MUST be: (1) exception-handling middleware (UseExceptionHandler / global error handler from this story) registered FIRST as the outermost layer; (2) correlation-id middleware (STORY-10.3) registered second; (3) health endpoints (MapHealthChecks) mapped next — they resolve before authentication so they are always reachable; (4) UseRouting; (5) UseAuthentication / UseAuthorization. The health endpoints bypass auth because they are mapped before UseAuthentication. The error handler wraps everything including health checks.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Per-exception mapping to specific 4xx codes (e.g. mapping NotFoundException → 404) — that is domain-error translation handled per-use-case in later epics.</li><li>Sentry capture of errors (STORY-10.4 layers that on top of the structured log entry produced here).</li><li>Retry / circuit-breaker logic (resilience patterns are out of scope for v1.0).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.2</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> any request to the API triggers an unhandled exception (null reference, unexpected domain error, infrastructure failure) <b>When</b> the global error handler catches it <b>Then</b> the response is an RFC 7807 problem-details body (application/problem+json) with at minimum type, title, status, and traceId fields; the status is 500; no stack trace, no exception message, no internal type name, and no PII is included in the response body.</p><p><b>Given</b> the error handler produces a 500 response <b>When</b> the response is serialized <b>Then</b> the traceId field value matches the X-Correlation-Id response header on that same request (set by STORY-10.3's middleware, or a fallback HttpContext.TraceIdentifier if 10.3 is not yet merged).</p><p><b>Given</b> an unhandled exception is caught <b>When</b> the handler logs it <b>Then</b> it logs at Error level with the full exception (message + stack) in the structured log sink, keyed by the same correlation id — the stack trace is in the logs, never in the response.</p><p><b>Given</b> an OperationCanceledException or TaskCanceledException is thrown because the client disconnected <b>When</b> the error handler processes it <b>Then</b> it returns 499 (or swallows cleanly without a 500) and logs at Information or Warning level — not Error.</p><p><b>Given</b> any error response is produced <b>When</b> a client parses it <b>Then</b> the Content-Type is application/problem+json and the body is valid JSON conforming to RFC 7807 (the shape all other epics' error ACs depend on).</p><p><b>Given</b> the API is running normally with no unhandled exceptions <b>When</b> requests succeed <b>Then</b> the error handler adds no observable overhead (it is middleware, not a try/catch on every endpoint).</p>"
```

### User Story — STORY-10.3: Structured logging with correlation id
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-10 → <EPIC-10-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-10; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As an on-call engineer, I want every API request to carry a consistent correlation id through all log entries — with structured, levelled output and no secrets or PII — so that I can trace the full lifecycle of any request from a single search in the log sink.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Correlation middleware is registered before UseAuthentication and UseAuthorization so the id is available on all requests including 401/403 responses.</li><li>The middleware reads and propagates a caller-supplied X-Correlation-Id; it does not require one. Downstream services (SignalR hub, background jobs) pass the id through ILogger scope.</li><li>No secrets/PII in logs is a hard constraint, not best-effort. Confirm by asserting in tests that the structured log sink never contains 'password', 'token', or 'connstr' property keys.</li><li>Logging configuration (sink, level, output format) lives in appsettings.json / appsettings.{Environment}.json — not hard-coded in Program.cs beyond bootstrapping.</li><li>Clean Architecture: ILogger&lt;T&gt; is used throughout Application and Infrastructure (it is a Microsoft abstraction acceptable in Application per the framework conventions); no Serilog/Sentry types in Domain or Application.</li><li>Log entries for health probe endpoints (/health, /health/ready) may be suppressed or throttled to avoid log noise from frequent load-balancer pings (configurable, default: suppress Information from health-check middleware).</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Distributed tracing (ActivitySource, OpenTelemetry) — correlation id via header propagation is sufficient for v1.0.</li><li>Log shipping infrastructure (Log Analytics workspace, Elastic, etc.) — the sink target is Sentry (STORY-10.4) and the local console in development; cloud log aggregation beyond Sentry is a future concern.</li><li>Request/response body logging (risk of PII capture).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.10</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> any inbound HTTP request <b>When</b> it passes through the correlation middleware <b>Then</b> a correlation id is assigned: if the request carries an X-Correlation-Id header with a non-empty value that header's value is used; otherwise a new Guid is generated. The id is attached to the ILogger scope for the duration of the request and echoed in an X-Correlation-Id response header.</p><p><b>Given</b> a correlation id is active <b>When</b> any ILogger call is made inside that request's scope (controllers, use-case handlers, infrastructure services) <b>Then</b> the structured log entry includes a CorrelationId property matching the request's id — no additional per-call instrumentation required from feature code.</p><p><b>Given</b> the application is configured for structured logging (Serilog or Microsoft.Extensions.Logging with a structured sink) <b>When</b> a log entry is emitted <b>Then</b> it is in JSON/structured format (not plain-text concatenation) with at minimum Timestamp, Level, CorrelationId, Message, and for request-scoped entries RequestPath and StatusCode.</p><p><b>Given</b> log entries are written <b>When</b> any entry is inspected <b>Then</b> it contains no connection strings, JWT tokens, bearer values, Key Vault URIs, passwords, or PII (user email addresses, names). Structured properties from sensitive inputs are excluded or masked at the logging layer.</p><p><b>Given</b> log levels are configured <b>When</b> the application runs in production <b>Then</b> Information and above are emitted; Debug/Trace are suppressed unless explicitly overridden by configuration. Level overrides are config-driven (appsettings.json / environment variable), not code-driven.</p><p><b>Given</b> Sentry is integrated (STORY-10.4) <b>When</b> it is configured <b>Then</b> the structured log entries feed Sentry breadcrumbs automatically via the SDK's AddSentry() log sink integration — no additional instrumentation needed beyond registering the sink.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-10.3: Structured logging with correlation id" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-10; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As an on-call engineer, I want every API request to carry a consistent correlation id through all log entries — with structured, levelled output and no secrets or PII — so that I can trace the full lifecycle of any request from a single search in the log sink.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Correlation middleware is registered before UseAuthentication and UseAuthorization so the id is available on all requests including 401/403 responses.</li><li>The middleware reads and propagates a caller-supplied X-Correlation-Id; it does not require one. Downstream services (SignalR hub, background jobs) pass the id through ILogger scope.</li><li>No secrets/PII in logs is a hard constraint, not best-effort. Confirm by asserting in tests that the structured log sink never contains 'password', 'token', or 'connstr' property keys.</li><li>Logging configuration (sink, level, output format) lives in appsettings.json / appsettings.{Environment}.json — not hard-coded in Program.cs beyond bootstrapping.</li><li>Clean Architecture: ILogger&lt;T&gt; is used throughout Application and Infrastructure (it is a Microsoft abstraction acceptable in Application per the framework conventions); no Serilog/Sentry types in Domain or Application.</li><li>Log entries for health probe endpoints (/health, /health/ready) may be suppressed or throttled to avoid log noise from frequent load-balancer pings (configurable, default: suppress Information from health-check middleware).</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Distributed tracing (ActivitySource, OpenTelemetry) — correlation id via header propagation is sufficient for v1.0.</li><li>Log shipping infrastructure (Log Analytics workspace, Elastic, etc.) — the sink target is Sentry (STORY-10.4) and the local console in development; cloud log aggregation beyond Sentry is a future concern.</li><li>Request/response body logging (risk of PII capture).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.10</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> any inbound HTTP request <b>When</b> it passes through the correlation middleware <b>Then</b> a correlation id is assigned: if the request carries an X-Correlation-Id header with a non-empty value that header's value is used; otherwise a new Guid is generated. The id is attached to the ILogger scope for the duration of the request and echoed in an X-Correlation-Id response header.</p><p><b>Given</b> a correlation id is active <b>When</b> any ILogger call is made inside that request's scope (controllers, use-case handlers, infrastructure services) <b>Then</b> the structured log entry includes a CorrelationId property matching the request's id — no additional per-call instrumentation required from feature code.</p><p><b>Given</b> the application is configured for structured logging (Serilog or Microsoft.Extensions.Logging with a structured sink) <b>When</b> a log entry is emitted <b>Then</b> it is in JSON/structured format (not plain-text concatenation) with at minimum Timestamp, Level, CorrelationId, Message, and for request-scoped entries RequestPath and StatusCode.</p><p><b>Given</b> log entries are written <b>When</b> any entry is inspected <b>Then</b> it contains no connection strings, JWT tokens, bearer values, Key Vault URIs, passwords, or PII (user email addresses, names). Structured properties from sensitive inputs are excluded or masked at the logging layer.</p><p><b>Given</b> log levels are configured <b>When</b> the application runs in production <b>Then</b> Information and above are emitted; Debug/Trace are suppressed unless explicitly overridden by configuration. Level overrides are config-driven (appsettings.json / environment variable), not code-driven.</p><p><b>Given</b> Sentry is integrated (STORY-10.4) <b>When</b> it is configured <b>Then</b> the structured log entries feed Sentry breadcrumbs automatically via the SDK's AddSentry() log sink integration — no additional instrumentation needed beyond registering the sink.</p>"
```

### User Story — STORY-10.4: Sentry integration (backend + SPA + CI source maps)
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-10 → <EPIC-10-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-10; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As an on-call engineer, I want unhandled errors from both the API and the Vue SPA captured automatically in Sentry — with de-minified traces (source maps uploaded by CI) and a Sentry alert wired as the incident.opened signal — so that production incidents are surfaced immediately and traceable to source.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Backend SDK: Sentry.AspNetCore — registered via UseSentry() in Program.cs; automatic capture of unhandled exceptions; SendDefaultPii = false (no PII in Sentry payloads).</li><li>SPA SDK: @sentry/vue — initialised in main.ts after app = createApp(App); DSN read from window.__config.sentryDsn (populated from runtime config.json); graceful no-op when DSN is absent/empty.</li><li>DSN handling: backend DSN = app setting / Key Vault reference (managed identity); SPA DSN = ingestion-scoped, public, in config.json. Neither DSN value is in source code or committed configuration files.</li><li>Release tracking: CI pipeline sets SENTRY_RELEASE to the build number or commit SHA; both sentry-cli upload steps reference the same value so front-end and back-end events are grouped to one release in Sentry.</li><li>Source maps: Vite build produces source maps; CI uploads them to Sentry after building and before deploying; the dist/ source maps are not served publicly (deleted or excluded from the frontend App Service deploy artifact after upload).</li><li>SendDefaultPii = false: confirmed in both SDK initialisations; user email/IP are not captured in Sentry events unless explicitly opt-in in a future story.</li><li>Clean Architecture: Sentry SDK is referenced only from the Api project (backend) and src/main.ts (SPA); no Sentry import in Domain, Application, or SPA component files.</li><li>incident.opened mechanism: Sentry alert rule → WEBHOOK → API receiver endpoint (POST /internal/sentry-webhook) authenticated with SENTRY_WEBHOOK_SECRET → receiver calls metrics-log.sh incident.opened. This is the only path; no CI-script alternative exists. The secret is stored as an app setting / Key Vault reference and never committed to source.</li><li>Source-map upload soft gate: sentry-cli upload failure is non-fatal; the pipeline emits a warning and proceeds. The CI step must use continue-on-error: true (or equivalent) so an upload failure never blocks a deploy.</li><li>The incident.opened alert binding is a one-alert, one-signal binding; complex alert routing is out of scope.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Sentry performance monitoring / tracing (transactions, spans) — error capture only in v1.0.</li><li>User-feedback prompts on crash (Sentry's user-feedback widget).</li><li>Multiple Sentry environments beyond production and development (staging is additive).</li><li>Alert routing beyond the single incident.opened signal (PagerDuty, Slack, etc.).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.10, ADR-000 R3</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> the API is configured with a Sentry DSN <b>When</b> an unhandled exception is caught by the global error handler (STORY-10.2) <b>Then</b> Sentry.CaptureException is called (via Sentry.AspNetCore automatic capture or explicit call), the event appears in the Sentry project, and the event's tags include the CorrelationId from STORY-10.3's scope.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API starts without a Sentry DSN configured (env variable absent or empty) <b>When</b> the process starts <b>Then</b> the application starts normally, logs a Warning-level entry ('Sentry DSN not configured — error capture disabled'), and handles all requests as normal — Sentry being absent does not crash or degrade the API.</p><p><b>Given</b> the backend Sentry DSN <b>When</b> it is read at startup <b>Then</b> it is sourced from the SENTRY_DSN app setting (or Key Vault reference via managed identity) — the value never appears in source code, appsettings.json, or any build artifact.</p><p><b>Given</b> the Vue SPA is loaded in a browser <b>When</b> the @sentry/vue SDK is initialised <b>Then</b> it reads the Sentry DSN from the runtime config.json (fetched at boot, not baked into the bundle), initialises with Vue.config.errorHandler wired, and captures unhandled Vue errors and promise rejections.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA DSN is public <b>When</b> the SPA bundle is inspected or config.json is fetched <b>Then</b> the DSN is an ingestion-scoped token (write-only; no read or admin scope) — confirming that leaking it does not expose event data.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA encounters an unhandled error caught by the @sentry/vue error handler <b>When</b> the error event is sent to Sentry <b>Then</b> the Sentry event includes a de-minified stack trace because CI has uploaded the source map for that release.</p><p><b>Given</b> a CI build succeeds and produces a release <b>When</b> the pipeline completes the deploy step <b>Then</b> the pipeline runs sentry-cli releases new &lt;version&gt; and sentry-cli releases files &lt;version&gt; upload-sourcemaps ./dist (or the equivalent Sentry Azure Pipelines task), associating the release with the deployed artifact version.</p><p><b>Given</b> a Sentry alert is configured to fire when the first occurrence of any new issue appears in the production environment <b>When</b> that alert fires <b>Then</b> Sentry's alert rule delivers a WEBHOOK to a dedicated receiver endpoint hosted in the API (e.g. POST /internal/sentry-webhook); the receiver authenticates the request via a shared-secret header (SENTRY_WEBHOOK_SECRET); the receiver invokes metrics-log.sh incident.opened (or equivalent in-process call), producing an incident.opened event in the metrics ledger — connecting Sentry to the spine's change-failure producer. There is no 'or pipeline script' alternative: the webhook→receiver→metrics-log.sh path is the sole mechanism.</p><p><b>Given</b> the sentry-cli source-map upload step runs in CI <b>When</b> the upload fails (network error, invalid token, Sentry API unavailable) <b>Then</b> the deploy pipeline continues — the source-map upload is a SOFT gate; the pipeline logs a warning-level entry ('Sentry source-map upload failed — this release's traces will be minified until re-uploaded'); the deploy artifact is still promoted; a re-upload can be triggered manually once the issue is resolved. The deploy MUST NOT be blocked by a monitoring-tooling failure.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA's @sentry/vue integration is active <b>When</b> the application transitions between routes <b>Then</b> Sentry records a breadcrumb for each navigation so that the event context shows the user's path before an error.</p>
```

**Create**
```
az boards work-item create --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --project taskflow --type "User Story" --title "STORY-10.4: Sentry integration (backend + SPA + CI source maps)" --area "taskflow" --iteration "taskflow" --fields "System.State=New" "System.Tags=EPIC-10; spec-traced" "System.Description=<p>As an on-call engineer, I want unhandled errors from both the API and the Vue SPA captured automatically in Sentry — with de-minified traces (source maps uploaded by CI) and a Sentry alert wired as the incident.opened signal — so that production incidents are surfaced immediately and traceable to source.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>Backend SDK: Sentry.AspNetCore — registered via UseSentry() in Program.cs; automatic capture of unhandled exceptions; SendDefaultPii = false (no PII in Sentry payloads).</li><li>SPA SDK: @sentry/vue — initialised in main.ts after app = createApp(App); DSN read from window.__config.sentryDsn (populated from runtime config.json); graceful no-op when DSN is absent/empty.</li><li>DSN handling: backend DSN = app setting / Key Vault reference (managed identity); SPA DSN = ingestion-scoped, public, in config.json. Neither DSN value is in source code or committed configuration files.</li><li>Release tracking: CI pipeline sets SENTRY_RELEASE to the build number or commit SHA; both sentry-cli upload steps reference the same value so front-end and back-end events are grouped to one release in Sentry.</li><li>Source maps: Vite build produces source maps; CI uploads them to Sentry after building and before deploying; the dist/ source maps are not served publicly (deleted or excluded from the frontend App Service deploy artifact after upload).</li><li>SendDefaultPii = false: confirmed in both SDK initialisations; user email/IP are not captured in Sentry events unless explicitly opt-in in a future story.</li><li>Clean Architecture: Sentry SDK is referenced only from the Api project (backend) and src/main.ts (SPA); no Sentry import in Domain, Application, or SPA component files.</li><li>incident.opened mechanism: Sentry alert rule → WEBHOOK → API receiver endpoint (POST /internal/sentry-webhook) authenticated with SENTRY_WEBHOOK_SECRET → receiver calls metrics-log.sh incident.opened. This is the only path; no CI-script alternative exists. The secret is stored as an app setting / Key Vault reference and never committed to source.</li><li>Source-map upload soft gate: sentry-cli upload failure is non-fatal; the pipeline emits a warning and proceeds. The CI step must use continue-on-error: true (or equivalent) so an upload failure never blocks a deploy.</li><li>The incident.opened alert binding is a one-alert, one-signal binding; complex alert routing is out of scope.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Sentry performance monitoring / tracing (transactions, spans) — error capture only in v1.0.</li><li>User-feedback prompts on crash (Sentry's user-feedback widget).</li><li>Multiple Sentry environments beyond production and development (staging is additive).</li><li>Alert routing beyond the single incident.opened signal (PagerDuty, Slack, etc.).</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §2.10, ADR-000 R3</p>" "Microsoft.VSTS.Common.AcceptanceCriteria=<p><b>Given</b> the API is configured with a Sentry DSN <b>When</b> an unhandled exception is caught by the global error handler (STORY-10.2) <b>Then</b> Sentry.CaptureException is called (via Sentry.AspNetCore automatic capture or explicit call), the event appears in the Sentry project, and the event's tags include the CorrelationId from STORY-10.3's scope.</p><p><b>Given</b> the API starts without a Sentry DSN configured (env variable absent or empty) <b>When</b> the process starts <b>Then</b> the application starts normally, logs a Warning-level entry ('Sentry DSN not configured — error capture disabled'), and handles all requests as normal — Sentry being absent does not crash or degrade the API.</p><p><b>Given</b> the backend Sentry DSN <b>When</b> it is read at startup <b>Then</b> it is sourced from the SENTRY_DSN app setting (or Key Vault reference via managed identity) — the value never appears in source code, appsettings.json, or any build artifact.</p><p><b>Given</b> the Vue SPA is loaded in a browser <b>When</b> the @sentry/vue SDK is initialised <b>Then</b> it reads the Sentry DSN from the runtime config.json (fetched at boot, not baked into the bundle), initialises with Vue.config.errorHandler wired, and captures unhandled Vue errors and promise rejections.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA DSN is public <b>When</b> the SPA bundle is inspected or config.json is fetched <b>Then</b> the DSN is an ingestion-scoped token (write-only; no read or admin scope) — confirming that leaking it does not expose event data.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA encounters an unhandled error caught by the @sentry/vue error handler <b>When</b> the error event is sent to Sentry <b>Then</b> the Sentry event includes a de-minified stack trace because CI has uploaded the source map for that release.</p><p><b>Given</b> a CI build succeeds and produces a release <b>When</b> the pipeline completes the deploy step <b>Then</b> the pipeline runs sentry-cli releases new &lt;version&gt; and sentry-cli releases files &lt;version&gt; upload-sourcemaps ./dist (or the equivalent Sentry Azure Pipelines task), associating the release with the deployed artifact version.</p><p><b>Given</b> a Sentry alert is configured to fire when the first occurrence of any new issue appears in the production environment <b>When</b> that alert fires <b>Then</b> Sentry's alert rule delivers a WEBHOOK to a dedicated receiver endpoint hosted in the API (e.g. POST /internal/sentry-webhook); the receiver authenticates the request via a shared-secret header (SENTRY_WEBHOOK_SECRET); the receiver invokes metrics-log.sh incident.opened (or equivalent in-process call), producing an incident.opened event in the metrics ledger — connecting Sentry to the spine's change-failure producer. There is no 'or pipeline script' alternative: the webhook→receiver→metrics-log.sh path is the sole mechanism.</p><p><b>Given</b> the sentry-cli source-map upload step runs in CI <b>When</b> the upload fails (network error, invalid token, Sentry API unavailable) <b>Then</b> the deploy pipeline continues — the source-map upload is a SOFT gate; the pipeline logs a warning-level entry ('Sentry source-map upload failed — this release's traces will be minified until re-uploaded'); the deploy artifact is still promoted; a re-upload can be triggered manually once the issue is resolved. The deploy MUST NOT be blocked by a monitoring-tooling failure.</p><p><b>Given</b> the SPA's @sentry/vue integration is active <b>When</b> the application transitions between routes <b>Then</b> Sentry records a breadcrumb for each navigation so that the event context shows the user's path before an error.</p>"
```

**Link to parent**
```
az boards work-item relation add --organization https://dev.azure.com/bitbodhi --id <this-story-id> --relation-type parent --target-id <EPIC-10-id>
```

---

### User Story — STORY-10.5: SPA reliability audit — loading/empty/error states + WCAG 2.2 AA sweep
- **Type:** User Story · **Parent:** EPIC-10 → <EPIC-10-id>
- **Area:** taskflow · **Iteration:** taskflow · **State:** New · **Tags:** EPIC-10; spec-traced

**Description (HTML)**
```html
<p>As an on-call engineer validating demo-readiness (and as an end-user), I want a time-boxed Definition-of-Done audit sweep across every SPA view — confirming that loading/empty/error states and WCAG 2.2 AA requirements (already mandated in each UI story's own ACs) are consistently implemented — so that the application is shippable and no view was silently skipped during EPIC-0 through EPIC-9 delivery.</p><p><b>NFR / constraints:</b></p><ul><li>This story is a time-boxed Definition-of-Done audit sweep (max 3 days / 1 spike). It is NOT a new feature and NOT a re-implementation. Findings of non-compliance result in new bug stories — they do not expand this story's scope.</li><li>Sprint-planning decomposition: produce a per-view checklist (view × {loading, empty, error} × WCAG gate); each row is a pass/fail audit result. The checklist is the deliverable.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AA is the floor — specifically SC 1.4.3 (contrast), SC 1.4.11 (non-text contrast), SC 2.4.7 (focus visible), SC 2.4.11 (focus not obscured, AA in 2.2), SC 2.5.3 (label in name), SC 4.1.3 (status messages).</li><li>Loading, empty, and error states must be implemented consistently using a shared composition (useAsync composable or Pinia store convention) rather than ad-hoc per-component flags, to prevent divergence as new views are added.</li><li>Error messages shown to users must be derived from the RFC 7807 title field (if available) or a generic localised string — never the raw detail or exception message.</li><li>The traceId support reference from RFC 7807 is surfaced as a copy-to-clipboard element, not a link, since it is not a URL.</li><li>Automated accessibility testing: Lighthouse accessibility score &gt;= 90 is the CI hard gate (per §2.7); this story must not regress below that threshold. Manual keyboard and screen-reader spot-checks supplement automation for dialog focus trap and aria-live announcements.</li><li>No external design comp — the UX spec in the story is the design reference.</li></ul><p><b>Out of scope:</b></p><ul><li>Adding new views or features; this story modifies existing views only.</li><li>Internationalisation (i18n) of error strings — English only for v1.0.</li><li>Offline / service-worker support.</li><li>WCAG 2.2 AAA criteria.</li></ul><p><b>Traces:</b> §1.6, §1.2 ('loading/empty/error states'), §2.9 (traceId from RFC 7807 responses surfaced in UI)</p>
```

**Acceptance Criteria (HTML)**
```html
<p><b>Given</b> any SPA view that fetches remote data (board list, board detail, card detail, 'My Tasks', search results) <b>When</b> the fetch is in progress <b>Then</b> a loading indicator is visible (skeleton screen, spinner, or progress region); the indicator is announced to screen readers via aria-busy='true' or an aria-live='polite' region; the interactive controls that depend on the data are disabled or absent while loading.</p><p><b>Given</b> any SPA view that fetches remote data <b>When</b> the API returns an empty collection or the resource does not exist <b>Then</b> a contextually appropriate empty-state message is shown ('No boards yet', 'No cards in this list', etc.) with a primary call-to-action where applicable (e.g. 'Create your first board'); the empty state is not a blank screen.</p><p><b>Given</b> any SPA view that fetches remote data <b>When</b> the API returns a 4xx or 5xx response, or the network request fails <b>Then</b> an error state is shown with a human-readable message, a retry action, and — for errors that include an RFC 7807 traceId — the trace id surfaced as copy-able support reference; no raw JSON, stack trace, or internal error detail is displayed to the user.</p><p><b>Given</b> an error state is displayed <b>When</b> a screen reader traverses the page <b>Then</b> the error message region has role='alert' or is an aria-live='assertive' region so the message is announced immediately on appearance.</p><p><b>Given</b> any interactive element across all SPA views (form field, button, link, modal, drag-and-drop handle) <b>When</b> audited against WCAG 2.2 AA <b>Then</b> it passes: keyboard navigability (Tab/Shift-Tab/Enter/Space/Esc/arrow keys); visible focus indicator (CSS :focus-visible with &gt;=3:1 contrast on the focus ring); colour contrast &gt;=4.5:1 for normal text (&gt;=3:1 for large text and UI components); no information conveyed by colour alone; form inputs have programmatically associated &lt;label&gt; elements; error messages are associated via aria-describedby.</p><p><b>Given</b> a destructive action (delete board, delete card, remove member) <b>When</b> the user triggers it <b>Then</b> a confirmation dialog appears; the dialog is a modal with role='dialog', aria-modal='true', a visible title (aria-labelledby), and focus trapped inside; Esc cancels; confirming calls the API; the dialog closes after the action completes or errors.</p><p><b>Given</b> the Sentry SPA integration (STORY-10.4) is active <b>When</b> an unhandled Vue component error surfaces the error state <b>Then</b> the component's onErrorCaptured hook (or the global app.config.errorHandler) captures the error to Sentry before rendering the error state — no silent swallowing.</p><p><b>Given</b> an error state includes a traceId support reference <b>When</b> the user activates the copy-to-clipboard action <b>AND</b> the Clipboard API is unavailable (non-secure context, navigator.clipboard absent, or the permission is denied) <b>Then</b> the copy button is replaced by (or falls back to) a selectable, focusable &lt;input readonly&gt; or &lt;pre tabindex='0'&gt; element containing the trace id so the user can manually select and copy it; the fallback element has a visible label ('Support reference — select to copy') and is keyboard-reachable.</p>
```

**Create**
